### Photon Capital (@PhotonCap)
_Fri Jul 17 16:55:30 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 40 · ↻ 3 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/PhotonCap/status/2078161683923841073)

> Silicon cannot make light.
>
> You can build the modulators, waveguides, and detectors in silicon, but the light source still has to come from InP. So the more silicon photonics wins, the more InP sells. What looks like a materials war is a vertical division of labor.
>
> UMC and Tower both expanding 300mm on the same day just pulled that trade forward. The math is in the piece.
> $COHR $LITE $MTSI $AXTI

### Athu (@athuinvests)
_Fri Jul 17 19:16:58 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 81 · ↻ 4 · 💬 13 · [open on X](https://x.com/athuinvests/status/2078197286103113912)

> Portfolio up 45% YTD, down from the ATHs.
>
> The pullback has given me plenty of lessons that I’ll carry into the next leg up.
>
> A few I wanted to share:
>
> - Set a strict limit on % allocation to any single stock, even if conviction is 120%, mainly due to volatility and risks. Allocate more to less volatile or revenue-proven names. Big lesson on BALANCE.
>
> Example: $SIVE at 110 SEK felt fairly valued to me, and hitting my fair value range without trimming let it reach 40% of the portfolio. I’m still reflecting on that. As a 2027+ long, I stopped buying until 30 SEK recently. Would like a second opinion?
>
> - Know when to trim or add—not perfectly, since you can’t time the market—but having a process helps manage risk and allocate better (especially during bad sentiment periods like recently). Also keep more cash on hand. Big lesson on PATIENCE for me.
>
> Example: Could have added $AAOI lower than the $140–$150s. With $KXIAY, I could have added more slowly instead of all in during the dips (in terms of allocated capital). Lack of basic TA skills (which I’m building now) would have helped.
>
> That said, I remain heavily invested in the AI buildout and concentrated in a few sectors with stocks at 2x+ potential.
>
> That’s the risk I’m willing to take personally.
>
> Names:
> - Cloud: $NBIS, $BRUN
> - Compute/Packaging/Foundry: $INTC
> - Memory: $MU, $KXIAY, $MIRAE (Equipment/Test)
> - Photonics: $SIVE, $AAOI
>
> Decided that materials won’t be in my portfolio for now (no $AXTI, $SOI, etc.), unless I do swing trades. 👀 But still looking into an energy long. 😉
>
> In terms of diversification, I am opening up to another tech area like software/fintech or defense/space.
>
> Mag7? Not right now. Still young enough to take more risk.
>
> But again, tech or nothing! Mainly because I want to invest where I’m 120% convinced and understand the sector properly.

### Gaetano (@crux_capital_)
_Fri Jul 17 19:53:00 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 42 · ↻ 1 · 💬 5 · [open on X](https://x.com/crux_capital_/status/2078206352414110036)

> Alright, let's start with $VIAV
>
> Market cap: ~$9.2B
> Next-quarter guide: ~$432M (+6.2% QoQ, +48.7% YoY)
> Next-12M revenue: $1.80-1.95B, 32-43% growth
> Exit margins: 63-64.5% gross, 24-26% operating
>
> VIAVI sits in the test layer for the optical buildout
>
> They touch many different stages of testing
>
> > During lab and product development
> > During manufacturing and production
> > During installation, operating, and field management
>
> They have very broad exposure in the data center:
>
> > Traditional pluggables
> > LPO, LRO, NPO, CPO, XPO 
> > AECs 
> > Retimers
> > PCIe 
> > CXL 
> > Hollow Core Fiber
>
> So they can test the silicon-photonics component, the optical engine, the packaged module, the Ethernet system, the physical fiber network, and the live AI fabric.
>
> One thing that I really like is that complexity increases test intensity. CPO, NPO, and advanced packaging create more testing insertions per system, so they can grow from both higher network volumes and more test content attached to each build.
>
> Also their Network and Service Enablement (NSE) segment has gross margins above 65%, with management estimating that roughly 40–45 cents of each incremental revenue dollar can reach operating profit.
>
> Some risks: Spirent integration, weak cash conversion/dilution, multiple compression, and delays in 1.6T/CPO customer ramps.
>
> *Reported growth includes the acquired Spirent product lines, which contributed $54.2 million last quarter, so don’t treat all of that growth as organic.
> *Margins / Rev are my projections 
>
> NFA

> An AI chokepoint portfolio down 49.4% this month. Every name hit $MU, MRVL, AAOI, SIVE, LITE all -30% to -50%.
>
> The bear circle jerk:
> - "AI is a bubble" - revenue doubling YoY, demand consuming every available wafer
> - "memory is a bubble" - HBM supply constrained with no relief until 2028
> - "photonics is a bubble" - optical chokepoints single-sourced, capacity sold out through 2029
> - "neoclouds get replaced" - $1B+ LTAs signed with new AI labs. Customer diversification strengthens the thesis.
> - "humanoids won't get anywhere" - factory deployment is real, not a demo
>
> Retail and bots scream "sell everything." The structural agreements keep getting signed - MU with QCOM, NBIS with Reflection AI. The buildout continues.
>
> The liquidation cascades through leverage, not thesis quality. Same pattern played out during tariff scares. The drawdown is a liquidity event, not a thesis break.
>
> Revenue inflection compounds in H2 2027. It's 2026. The thesis doesn't break because the calendar hasn't caught up.
>
> TLDR: the market is pricing liquidation velocity, not revenue trajectory. The separation when the leverage clears is the trade.
>
> what's the bear case here?

### P Equity Research 📰 (@pequityresearch)
_Fri Jul 17 21:10:41 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 172 · ↻ 19 · 💬 13 · [open on X](https://x.com/pequityresearch/status/2078225902027108605)

> Morgan Stanley: Optical vs Copper
>
> How do you think about the optical scale up opportunity in 2027, 2028, 2029, etc, and how does that relates to the Nvidia ecosystem and roadmap?
>
> A: We believe a small scale out adoption next year, with small volumes accounting for 10-15% penetration with scale out. We do think there are some low adoption with CPO until Feynman in 2029. Small, single digit adoption of CPO in 2028 and really scaling in 2029.
>
> You took your TAM to $73B, 4x from a year ago, talk about the drivers of that and how that compares to consensus and buy side out there?
>
> A: Driven by CapEx data points being 2x we were expecting last year, that is one vector of growth. The other is the cluster sizes being discussed are the biggest rivers of scale up network . We have gone from 8 to 72, then from a couple 100s to 1000s in the next couple generations. This acts as a multiplier to scale up multiplier.
>
> Talk about the exposure among Lumentum, Coherent, and Corning. Are there nuances between who is more exposed, less exposed?
>
> A: For CPO within scale out, it is generally positive for Lumentum. Doesn't necessarily changed a whole lot for Corning. With Coherent, they have to balance it out with transceiver business they have. For Lumentum it is the most positive because of the one customer they have on the transceiver side being google and they are not going to be adopting CPO. For CPO within scale up, it is opportunity for all 3. This is where copper gets replaced with fiber and lit up by lasers and optical engines made by Coherent an Lumentum. In terms of overall exposure, Lumentum has a bigger catalyst because of larger AI/DC revenue. It would be incremental for both Coherent and lumentum. Lumentum #1, Coherent or Corning #2.
>
> Tell me about the Corning Glass Bridge announcement that got the stock excited?
>
> A: This is not a new announcement. It was a paper they released in 2025 and a presentation they did that refocused the market on this technology. It is already part of the $10B photonics target the company discussed couple of months ago.
>
> In terms of catalyst for optical space, OCP (Open Compute Project) coming in October has gone popular. What are you expecting to hear from this?
>
> A: We think this will be a catalyst because it provides more exposure into hyperscaler behavior. OCP will give us a chance to see hyperscalers roadmap, it will focus on CPO, NPO adoption and the vendors involved.
>
> Copper is still the story for 2026 and 2027. We have seen this continued enthusiasm for ASICs. How is copper well positioned for this dynamic? Who are the well positioned beneficiaries?
>
> A: Copper life can be extended with use of retimers and better SerDes. Copper has a lot of runway before switching to optics. We will likely see a hybrid environment before going to 100% optics. A large debate in scale up is what fabric and protocol will become dominant other than NVLINK as we get into new XPUs and alternatives to Nvidia GPUs ramping. A big debate here is between UALink and ethernet. Ethernet is dependent on Broadcom's new ASICs ramping in 2H2027 into 2028, we think Broadcom will have opportunity to bundle XPU solutions with networking portfolio and are very well positioned in ethernet. On UALink, this is high optionality for Marvell and Astera Labs. Astera has the scale up switch for Trainium 3, this is a PCIe based solution. We think customers will want to move to UA Link eventually.
>
> You consider Keysight as an agnostic winner in R&D, regardless of the copper vs optical timeline. Explain your thesis and why do you see it pulling ahead?
>
> A: Keysight really ways in multiple ways when it comes to AI. First, it benefits from different types of architectures being discussed which all need to be tested with their equipment in labs. Second, when you move to higher speeds (400g laser vs 200g), it requires more complicated testing. Third, when architectures change frequently, like every 2 years, that boosts their business. The variety of architectures being tested matters.
>
> $ALAB $NVDA $AVGO $MRVL $CRDO $SMTC $APH $KEYS $COHR $LITE $GLW $GOOGL

### Patrick (@TemptInvest)
_Fri Jul 17 21:52:18 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 27 · ↻ 3 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/TemptInvest/status/2078236375761977438)

> I want to say something about $NOK that most people aren’t saying.
>
> The world is about to move more data than it has in its entire history combined. 
>
> Not gradually. 
>
> Not over decades. 
>
> In the next four years. 
>
> Every AI model being trained, every inference request being served, every GPU talking to another GPU inside a hyperscale data center, all of it generates traffic that has to travel somewhere. 
>
> Through fiber. 
>
> Through optical transceivers. 
>
> Through routers. 
>
> Through radio networks smart enough to handle loads that didn’t exist three years ago.
>
> That infrastructure doesn’t build itself.
>
> And the company quietly sitting at the center of all of it, making the optical transceivers, the IP routers, the radio access networks, and now an AI native 6G platform launched not to long ago,  is a Finnish company that most people dismissed a decade ago and haven’t looked at seriously since.
>
> Here’s what changed.
>
> Nokia booked €1 billion in AI and cloud orders in a single quarter. JPMorgan just raised their target from $14 to $21. Nvidia invested $1 billion at $6.01 a share, a price the stock has since blown past. AI and cloud revenue grew 49% year over year last quarter. Optical networks up 20%. Operating profit beat estimates by 12%. Guidance raised. Network Infrastructure growth forecast doubled.
>
> Two days ago Nokia launched its AI RAN platform, a radio access network built natively for artificial intelligence that thinks and adapts in real time. Their CEO called it one of the most significant advancements in radio technology in decades.
>
> And Nokia makes their own indium phosphide lasers in house. In Pennsylvania. In a facility just expanded 10x. Every competitor buys their lasers. Nokia makes theirs. That distinction matters more every quarter as supply chain sovereignty becomes a national priority.
>
> Q2 earnings are July 23rd. Six days away. First report where the Nvidia partnership shows up in order books. First report where the Allentown photonics expansion starts contributing. First look at whether the €1 billion in Q1 optical orders is the floor or the ceiling.
>
> The data has to move somewhere.
>
> I believe $NOK Nokia is where it moves.

### P Equity Research 📰 (@pequityresearch)
_Fri Jul 17 22:17:49 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 135 · ↻ 25 · 💬 2 · [open on X](https://x.com/pequityresearch/status/2078242798571049071)

> Goldman Sachs: Innolight & Optical Modules
>
> Market Trends and Technology Migration
>
> > Speed Evolution: The industry is aggressively migrating toward higher-speed optical modules. 1.6T modules are moving toward volume production as the next mainstream standard, while 3.2T optical modules are expected to begin volume ramp-up in 2027.
>
> > Silicon Photonics (SiPh) Dominance: Silicon photonics is increasingly displacing traditional EML-based solutions due to lower power consumption, superior performance, and simplified packaging.
>
> > Penetration Rates: By 2026, SiPh penetration is projected to reach 60% for 800G, 80% for 1.6T, and 100% for 3.2T products.
>
> > Revenue Share: Silicon photonics' share of total optical module revenue is expected to surge from 28% in 2025 to 62% by 2028.
>
> Innolight Shipment and Market Share Highlights
>
> > Leadership: Innolight is the leading supplier of 1.6T pluggable modules. It is projected to hold a 50–60% market share of 1.6T modules in 2026. Other industry reports indicate Innolight's market share for 1.6T modules may reach as high as 50–70%.
>
> 1.6T and 3.2T Outlook:
>
> > 1.6T: Expected to become the "absolute mainstream" by 2027, with 45.72 million units projected to be shipped that year.
>
> > 3.2T: Following the ramp-up of 1.6T, 3.2T shipments are expected to double in 2028 compared to their initial volume ramp year in 2027.
>
> > Manufacturing & Capacity: To support this demand, Innolight planned a 155% year-on-year increase in capital expenditure for 2026 to expand production capacity.
>
> Market Dynamics: Volume, Revenue, and ASP
>
> > Speed Migration (Volume Mix): The market is shifting rapidly from legacy "Below 400G" speeds toward high-speed AI-focused modules. 
>
> While "Below 400G" accounted for 89% of shipment volume in 2025, that share is projected to decline to 77% by 2028E. 
>
> Conversely, high-speed modules are capturing significant volume: 1.6T modules are projected to grow from 1% of volume in 2025 to 10% by 2028E, and 3.2T modules are expected to reach 5% of total shipment volume by 2028E.
>
> > Average Selling Price (ASP) Trends: The report explicitly notes an assumed year-over-year (YoY) ASP decline for "like-for-like" products. 
>
> For example, the ASP for 1.6T modules is expected to drop from $840 in 2025 to $435 by 2028E. 
>
> The 3.2T module, which enters the market in 2027, has a high starting ASP of $1,023 in 2027E, which is then projected to decline to $768 by 2028E.
>
> Technological Shift: SiPh vs. EML
>
> > Silicon Photonics (SiPh) Adoption: The market is undergoing a significant transition from traditional EML-based materials to Silicon Photonics.
>
> SiPh revenue penetration is expected to increase from 28% in 2025 to 62% by 2028E.
>
> Correspondingly, the SiPh penetration rate (by volume) is projected to climb from 6% in 2025 to 18% by 2028E.
>
> Market Opportunity (TAM)
>
> > Total Addressable Market (TAM): The global optical module TAM is expected to grow from $34.2 billion in 2025 to a peak of $72.6 billion in 2027E, before moderating slightly to $69.1 billion in 2028E.
>
> > High-Speed Revenue Growth: The 1.6T and 3.2T segments represent the primary growth engines, with combined revenue for these categories projected to grow from $3.9 billion in 2025 to $44.9 billion in 2028E.

### mark (@cherryPayment)
_Fri Jul 17 22:38:17 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 9 · ↻ 0 · 💬 6 · [open on X](https://x.com/cherryPayment/status/2078247946894622934)

> 我认为是很合理的分析
>
> 首先我们需要知道底层逻辑为什么英飞拓可以作为行业晴雨表？
>
> 我们要知道英飞拓是全球最大光模块厂商之一，它的ASP走势和出货量确实能反映整个产业链的景气度。高盛这样的机构是不会无缘无故上调108%/119%的盈利预测，那么其背后一定有channel check支撑。
>
> 所以基于此我是倾向于把英飞拓理解为光子行业的”台积电”。
>
> 而这个逻辑是台积电的资本开支指引和产能扩张节奏，是整个半导体行业景气度的先行指标；同理，英飞拓的订单结构、ASP走势和产能规划，是光子产业链景气度的先行指标。当英飞拓的盈利预测被机构上修超过100%，这不仅仅是一家公司的好消息——这是整个生态的信号弹。
>
> 800G超预期这个信号很关键。800G目前仍是主力交付速率，超预期意味着数据中心扩建节奏比市场预期快，这对LITE这类以800G为主的厂商是直接利好。
>
> 1.6T/3.2T拉高ASP的逻辑也成立，更高速率产品单价更高，即使出货量不变，收入和毛利都会改善。
>
> 高盛预期英飞拓在硅光（Silicon Photonics）模块的出货量将显著超出此前预期。这背后是三个维度的需求同步爆发：
>
> •Scale Out（横向扩展）：更多GPU集群节点互联，需要更多光模块
>
> •Scale Up（纵向扩展）：单节点算力密度提升，对高速互联带宽需求更高
>
> •Scale Across（跨域扩展）：数据中心之间、城域网之间的互联需求增加
> 这三个维度的同步扩张，意味着光模块不再只是某一个场景的刚需，而是AI算力基础设施全面扩张的基础组件。
>
> 2. 1.6T/3.2T产品拉高ASP和利润率
> 光模块产品的迭代路径是：400G → 800G → 1.6T → 3.2T。更高速率的产品，单价更高，毛利率通常也更好。
> 1.6T和3.2T产品的加速渗透，意味着即使英飞拓的出货量增速放缓，其收入和毛利仍会因为产品结构升级而显著改善。这是一个量价齐升的逻辑——在AI Capex持续扩张的背景下，这个趋势有望延续至2028年。
>
> 3. AI Capex的持续扩张
>
> 微软、Google、Meta、亚马逊等全球四大超大规模云厂商的2025年资本开支指引，无一例外都在大幅提升。这些资金最终会流向哪里？算力芯片、服务器、网络互联设备——以及连接这一切的光模块。
>
> 英飞拓作为这条链条中最关键的环节之一，是AI Capex最直接的受益者之一。
>
> 所以我认为在方向正确 + 间接收益方面 ：我是倾向于 $soi 和 $sive的

---

### Investor Denis (@InvestorDenis)
_Fri Jul 17 23:05:00 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 23 · ↻ 6 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/InvestorDenis/status/2078254671198638361)

> Just found new evidence the US government is dead serious about developing quantum technologies.
>
> US research is funded partly through the National Science Foundation (NSF). If your grant application is approved, you receive money.
>
> The NSF launched an initiative called NSF X-Labs two months ago. The goal of the initiative is to fund teams of researchers, engineers, and entrepreneurs to solve specific scientific challenges.
>
> The funding available is $1,5 billion over the next decade.
>
> The first round of X-Labs couldn’t have been more explicit. It invited proposals on two topics:
>
> 1/ Scientific instrumentation for sensing and imaging (deadline for grant applications: July 13)
>
> 2/ Quantum systems: Interconnects and integrated photonics (deadline July 20)
>
> The initiative resonates with
>
> 1/ the $2 billion direct equity investment into nine quantum companies in May
>
> 2/ the Executive Orders on quantum in June that look to find companies capable of providing these technologies, e.g. $INFQ and $IONQ.
>
> It’s hard not to be bullish on a technology pushed by the US government.

### นักลงพุง (@naklongpoong)
_Fri Jul 17 23:32:05 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/naklongpoong/status/2078261485424304227)

> ตลาด Optical Module กำลังเข้าสู่ยุค 1.6T และ 3.2T พร้อมแรงหนุนจาก Silicon Photonics
>
> Goldman Sachs ระบุว่า อุตสาหกรรม Optical Module กำลังเร่งเปลี่ยนผ่านไปสู่โมดูลความเร็วสูงเพื่อรองรับการเติบโตของ AI Data Center โดย 1.6T กำลังก้าวขึ้นเป็นมาตรฐานหลักของตลาด ขณะที่ 3.2T จะเริ่มเข้าสู่การผลิตจำนวนมากในปี 2027
>
> การเปลี่ยนผ่านสู่ Optical Module ความเร็วสูง
>
> อุตสาหกรรมกำลังเร่งเปลี่ยนจากโมดูลรุ่นเดิมไปสู่ความเร็วที่สูงขึ้น
>
> 1.6T กำลังเข้าสู่การผลิตจำนวนมาก และจะกลายเป็นมาตรฐานหลักของตลาด
> 3.2T คาดว่าจะเริ่มผลิตในระดับ Mass Production ตั้งแต่ปี 2027
> Silicon Photonics กำลังแทนที่ EML
>
> Goldman Sachs มองว่า Silicon Photonics (SiPh) จะเข้ามาแทนเทคโนโลยี EML (Electro-Absorption Modulated Laser) อย่างต่อเนื่อง เนื่องจากมีข้อได้เปรียบหลายด้าน ได้แก่
>
> ใช้พลังงานต่ำกว่า
> ประสิทธิภาพสูงกว่า
> กระบวนการประกอบแพ็กเกจง่ายกว่า
>
> อัตราการใช้งาน SiPh ที่คาดการณ์
> 800G: 60% ภายในปี 2026
> 1.6T: 80%
> 3.2T: 100%
>
> ขณะที่สัดส่วนรายได้ของ Silicon Photonics จะเพิ่มจาก 28% ในปี 2025 เป็น 62% ภายในปี 2028
>
> Innolight ครองตลาด 1.6T
>
> Goldman Sachs ระบุว่า Innolight เป็นผู้นำตลาด Optical Module แบบ 1.6T Pluggable
>
> คาดว่าจะมีส่วนแบ่งตลาด 50–60% ในปี 2026
>
> ขณะที่รายงานจากแหล่งอื่นประเมินว่าส่วนแบ่งตลาดอาจสูงถึง 50–70%
>
> แนวโน้ม 1.6T และ 3.2T
>
> 1.6T
> คาดว่าจะกลายเป็นมาตรฐานหลักของอุตสาหกรรมภายในปี 2027
> ยอดจัดส่งปี 2027 คาดอยู่ที่ 45.72 ล้านโมดูล
>
> 3.2T
> หลังจาก 1.6T เริ่มแพร่หลายแล้ว
> ยอดจัดส่ง 3.2T ในปี 2028 คาดว่าจะเพิ่มขึ้นเป็น 2 เท่า ของปีแรกที่เริ่มผลิตในปี 2027
>
> เพื่อรองรับความต้องการดังกล่าว Innolight วางแผนเพิ่ม CapEx ปี 2026 ถึง 155% YoY เพื่อขยายกำลังการผลิต
>
> การเปลี่ยนแปลงของตลาดและ ASP
>
> ตลาดกำลังเปลี่ยนจาก Optical Module ความเร็วต่ำ ไปสู่ผลิตภัณฑ์สำหรับ AI อย่างรวดเร็ว
>
> สัดส่วนยอดจัดส่ง
> โมดูลต่ำกว่า 400G จะลดจาก 89% ในปี 2025 เหลือ 77% ในปี 2028
> 1.6T จะเพิ่มจาก 1% เป็น 10%
> 3.2T จะเพิ่มเป็น 5% ของยอดจัดส่งทั้งหมดภายในปี 2028
>
> ด้านราคาขายเฉลี่ย (ASP)
> Goldman Sachs คาดว่าราคาจะปรับลดลงตามการผลิตจำนวนมาก
>
> 1.6Tปี 2025: 840 ดอลลาร์
> ปี 2028: 435 ดอลลาร์
>
> 3.2Tปี 2027: 1,023 ดอลลาร์
> ปี 2028: 768 ดอลลาร์
>
> การเปลี่ยนผ่านจาก EML ไปสู่ SiPh
> ตลาดกำลังเปลี่ยนผ่านจาก EML ไปสู่ Silicon Photonics อย่างชัดเจน
> สัดส่วนรายได้ของ SiPh จะเพิ่มจาก 28% ในปี 2025 เป็น 62% ในปี 2028
> ส่วนแบ่งการใช้งานตามปริมาณ (Volume Penetration) จะเพิ่มจาก 6% เป็น 18% ในช่วงเวลาเดียวกัน
>
> โอกาสของตลาด (TAM)
>
> Goldman Sachs คาดว่ามูลค่าตลาด Optical Module ทั่วโลกจะเติบโตอย่างแข็งแกร่ง
> 2025: 34.2 พันล้านดอลลาร์
> 2027: 72.6 พันล้านดอลลาร์ (จุดสูงสุด)
> 2028: 69.1 พันล้านดอลลาร์
>
> ขณะที่รายได้จากกลุ่ม 1.6T และ 3.2T ซึ่งเป็นแรงขับเคลื่อนหลักของอุตสาหกรรม จะเพิ่มจาก
> 3.9 พันล้านดอลลาร์ในปี 2025
> เป็น 44.9 พันล้านดอลลาร์ในปี 2028

> Citi: EML Output
>
> > Industry Shift Toward 200G and CW: Across almost all listed companies, there is a marked transition away from 100G EML production by 2028, with a significant ramp-up in both 200G EML and CW output.
>
> > AXT, Inc. Growth: AXT, Inc. shows a substantial increase in its 200G EML and CW output, with its 200G EML output projected to grow from 13.54 million chips in 2025 to 157.82 million chips by 2028.
>
> > Rapid Expansion in China: Companies such as Source Photonics (Dongshan Precision) and the "Other China" category show dramatic growth in CW output. Source Photonics, for example, is projected to increase its CW output from 14.66 million chips in 2025 to 161.77 million chips by 2028.
>
> > Sumitomo Electric: Sumitomo maintains high production levels, particularly in the 200G EML segment, which jumps from 28.93 million in 2025 to 128.58 million in 2028.

### Investify Daily (@InvestifyDaily)
_Sat Jul 18 14:16:00 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 9 · ↻ 0 · 💬 4 · [open on X](https://x.com/InvestifyDaily/status/2078483930668519933)

> BLUF: What is $LASE ?
>
> $LASE (Laser Photonics) develops industrial laser systems used for cleaning, cutting, marking, engraving, and surface preparation. Instead of chemicals or abrasive blasting, its technology uses high-powered lasers to remove rust, paint, coatings, and contaminants—serving markets like defense, aerospace, manufacturing, energy, and infrastructure.
>
> Bull Case: If laser cleaning continues replacing traditional methods, $LASE could benefit from a multi-year shift toward safer, faster, and more environmentally friendly industrial maintenance. Growth in defense spending, reshoring of manufacturing, and aging infrastructure all create potential demand. Long term, success depends on scaling revenue, expanding its product lineup, and proving its technology can win recurring commercial and government contracts.
>
> Bear Case: $LASE is still a very small company with limited revenue and faces execution risk. The industrial laser market is competitive, larger players have significantly more resources, and the company must consistently convert interest into meaningful sales. Until revenue growth and profitability become more predictable, the stock will likely remain highly volatile.
>
> Long term, this is an execution story—not a hype story. If management can consistently grow sales, secure larger contracts, and establish Laser Photonics as a leader in industrial laser cleaning, today’s valuation could look inexpensive. If execution stalls, however, the upside thesis becomes much harder to justify.

### Ze Dude (@ZeDude1510)
_Sat Jul 18 17:10:53 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 6 · ↻ 1 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/ZeDude1510/status/2078527943488499791)

> On vit une période très particulière pour les investisseurs en Semi en ce moment ...
>
> Je profite de ce moment pour faire un point sur les différents drawdown de ces dernières années et leurs causes 
>
> Que retrouvons-nous ? 
>
> Sur les 10 dernières années (2016 → mi-2026), $SOXX a connu 3 drawdowns majeurs de plus de 30 % 
>
> Voici le classement clair, du plus important au moins important, avec les dates, l’ampleur et les raisons principales :
>
> 1. 2021-2022 : -46,24 % (le plus gros)
> •Pic : fin décembre 2021 (~185 $)
> •Creux : 14 octobre 2022 (~99,56 $)
> •Durée : ~10 mois
> •Raisons principales :
> oSursaut d’inventaires après le boom COVID (les entreprises avaient trop stocké).
> oHausses agressives des taux de la Fed (de 0 % à plus de 5 %) pour combattre l’inflation → compression des valorisations des actions de croissance/tech.
> oRotation « growth → value » et craintes de récession.
> oCycle semi-conducteurs classique après une période de forte demande.
>
> 2. 2024-2025 : -41,67 % (2e plus gros)
> •Pic : 10 juillet 2024
> •Creux : 8 avril 2025
> •Durée : ~9 mois
> •Raisons principales :
> oPrise de bénéfices après les très fortes hausses liées à l’IA (Nvidia & co.).
> oInterrogations sur la soutenabilité des dépenses capex IA des hyperscalers (Microsoft, Google, Meta, Amazon) et le délai avant que ça se traduise en revenus réels.
> oTensions géopolitiques États-Unis/Chine : restrictions d’exportation de puces IA, tarifs potentiels sous Trump, charges importantes annoncées par Nvidia et AMD sur leurs ventes en Chine.
> oSurcapacité dans certains segments + demande plus faible hors IA (PC, smartphones).
> oRotation sectorielle temporaire et craintes de valorisations trop élevées après l’euphorie IA.
> C’est le drawdown le plus récent avant celui en cours (et presque aussi violent que celui de 2022).
>
> 3. 2020 (COVID) : -34,25 %
> •Pic : 19 février 2020
> •Creux : 20 mars 2020
> •Durée : seulement ~1 mois (très rapide)
> •Raisons principales :
> oCrash boursier mondial lié à la pandémie de Covid-19.
> oCraintes de confinement généralisé et d’arrêt de l’économie.
> oPerturbations des chaînes d’approvisionnement (même si le secteur s’est très vite redressé grâce à la demande digitale).
>
> 4.     2018 (Guerre commerciale) : -26,14 %
> oRaisons : guerre commerciale Trump-Chine, tarifs sur les produits tech, craintes de restrictions d’exportation de puces vers la Chine (Huawei, etc.).
>
> Synthèse sur 10 ans
> RangPériodeDrawdownDurée approx.Cause principale
> 12021-2022-46,2 %10 moisHausses taux + surstock
> 22024-2025-41,7 %9 moisIA + géopolitique Chine
> 32020-34,3 %1 moisCovid
> -2018-26,1 %~9 moisGuerre commerciale
>
> En rajoutant celui de cette année on retrouve cela : 
>
> Drawdowns majeurs de $SOXX sur les ~10-11 dernières années (2015 → 17 juillet 2026)
>
> RangPériodeDrawdownDurée approx.StatutRaisons principales
> 1Déc. 2021 – Oct. 2022-46,24 %~10 moisTerminéHausses agressives des taux Fed + surstock post-COVID + compression des valorisations tech
>
> 2Juil. 2024 – Avr. 2025-41,67 %~9 moisTerminéPrise de bénéfices IA, craintes sur la rentabilité des capex IA, restrictions export Chine (Nvidia/AMD), surcapacité partielle
>
> 3Fév. – Mars 2020-34,25 %~1 moisTerminéCrash Covid-19 (confinements mondiaux + peur d’arrêt économique)
>
> 4Mars 2018 – Déc. 2018-26,14 %~9 moisTerminéGuerre commerciale Trump-Chine + craintes de restrictions sur les exportations de puces
>
> 522 juin – 17 juil. 2026-20,34 %~25 joursEn coursReprise de profit + réévaluation des valorisations IA (attentes trop hautes sur la monétisation des capex), signaux techniques (possible death cross), concurrence chinoise (DeepSeek), et rotation sectorielle
>
> Points clés sur le drawdown d’aujourd’hui :
> •C’est le plus important des 12 derniers mois 
> •Il est encore modéré par rapport aux 3 plus gros des 10 dernières années.
> •Il est très récent et rapide (principalement concentré sur les 3-4 dernières semaines).
> •Raisons du moment : les investisseurs commencent à douter que les énormes dépenses en IA se traduisent rapidement en bénéfices concrets, avec en plus des tensions géopolitiques et des prises de bénéfices après la très forte hausse de 2025-2026.
>
> Maintenant, essayons de trouver du positif dans l’Histoire : combien de temps à revenir à l’ATH ? 
>
> Drawdowns majeurs de $SOXX (dernières ~11 années) + temps de récupération
>
> PériodeDrawdownDéclin (pic → creux)Récupération (creux → retour au pic précédent)Temps total (pic → retour au pic)Statut / Date de récupération
>
> Déc. 2021 – Oct. 2022-46,24 %291 jours (~9,5 mois)426 jours (~14 mois)717 jours (~1 an 11 mois)Récupéré le 14 déc. 2023
>
> Juil. 2024 – Avr. 2025-41,67 %272 jours (~9 mois)163 jours (~5,5 mois)435 jours (~14 mois)Récupéré le 18 sept. 2025
>
> Fév. – Mars 2020-34,25 %30 jours (~1 mois)77 jours (~2,5 mois)107 jours (~3,5 mois)Récupéré le 5 juin 2020
>
> 2018 (Guerre commerciale)-26,14 %287 jours (9,5 mois)100 jours (~3,3 mois)387 jours (~12,7 mois)Récupéré en avril 2019
>
> 22 juin – 17 juil. 2026 (actuel)-20,34 %25 joursEn coursEn coursToujours en drawdown (pas encore revenu au pic de juin 2026)
>
> Interprétation rapide :
> •Le plus long à récupérer : celui de 2021-2022 (presque 2 ans pour revenir au pic).
> •Le plus rapide : celui de 2020 (Covid) → seulement 2,5 mois de récupération grâce au rebond ultra-rapide.
> •Le plus récent terminé (2024-2025) : récupération relativement rapide (~5,5 mois).
> •Celui d’aujourd’hui : seulement 25 jours de déclin pour l’instant → beaucoup plus court que les gros drawdowns précédents, mais on ne sait pas encore combien de temps il mettra à se résorber.
>
> Note optimiste sur « revenir à ATH » : 
>
> Dans la plupart des cas, une fois revenu au pic précédent, le titre a rapidement fait un nouveau plus haut historique (sauf pendant les périodes très plates). Le temps indiqué ci-dessus est donc très proche du moment où il a refait un ATH.
>
> En résumé, les drawdown sur les Semi sont relativement fréquents, et le retour à l’ATH , même s’il prend du temps, est systématique sur les 10 dernières années 
>
> Ne perdez pas confiance, ne vendez pas au plus bas, tenez bon 
>
> The darkest hour is just before the dawn 
>

### CurioSphere (@CurioSphereX)
_Sat Jul 18 17:30:00 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 12 · ↻ 6 · 💬 3 · [open on X](https://x.com/CurioSphereX/status/2078532754677838234)

> 🚨: Scientists Discover a Fundamental Limit to Measuring an Electron in Space and Time ⚛️⏱️
>
> Researchers from the Regensburg Center for Ultrafast Nanoscopy and the Max Planck Institute have identified a new fundamental limit in quantum physics, showing that an electron's exact position and the precise moment it moves cannot both be measured with perfect accuracy.
>
> Published in Nature Photonics, the team used an ultrafast scanning tunneling microscope combined with advanced laser pulses to observe electrons tunneling across atomic-scale gaps. Their measurements revealed an intrinsic response delay of about 500 attoseconds (500 quintillionths of a second) between the arrival of light and the electron's motion.

### Eve Bodnia (@evelovesolive)
_Sat Jul 18 17:39:45 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 19 · ↻ 2 · 💬 4 · [open on X](https://x.com/evelovesolive/status/2078535207570010206)

> I love to see startup pitching theoretical discovery for market. Look at theoretical physics: SUSY is a beautiful theory which was proven not to be real by experiments on LHC. Experiments tell you what’s real and what’s not. You can create as many as you like ways to do quantum computing (and I did it myself during my PhD), but only lab will tell you what will be possible. If you really want to win discovery market, automate experiments instead: automate nanofabrication, photonics, chemistry in a physical way. Theory is not enough without experiments.

### aibottlenecks (@aibottlenecks)
_Sat Jul 18 17:50:45 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/aibottlenecks/status/2078537977819701344)

> Mid-Month Update: A Valuation Reset, Not a Thesis Reset
>
> The recent selloff has been uncomfortable, but it has also been clarifying.
>
> AI and semiconductor stocks entered July following an extraordinary first-half run. As valuations expanded, expectations left less room for uncertainty. The subsequent correction has been broad and sharp: the semiconductor index has fallen approximately 20% from its June peak, while investors reassess elevated valuations, the economics of AI spending, competition from more efficient Chinese models, and rising geopolitical risk.
>
> This portfolio was never designed to avoid these periods. It is an aggressive, concentrated strategy built around semiconductors, power infrastructure, grid equipment, cooling, and Bitcoin. Drawdowns of 40%–50% are possible over a full cycle, and the strategy should be evaluated over three-to-five-year periods - not several difficult weeks.
>
> The important question is not simply whether prices have declined. It is whether the underlying bottleneck thesis has deteriorated.
>
> So far, the evidence suggests that much of this move is a valuation reset rather than a fundamental thesis reset. TSMC recently reported record quarterly profits, raised its 2026 revenue outlook, and increased planned capital spending in response to continued AI-chip demand. That does not eliminate cyclicality or valuation risk, but it indicates that demand for advanced computing infrastructure remains substantial even as public-market sentiment has weakened.
>
> The portfolio continues to own the scarce inputs that competing AI systems must consume:
>
> * Advanced compute and high-bandwidth memory
> * EUV lithography and advanced packaging
> * Optical networking and photonics
> * Reliable electricity, cooling, and grid expansion
> * Bitcoin as a bounded digital-scarcity sleeve
>
> Lower-cost and more efficient AI models deserve careful attention. They could pressure individual software companies and alter the economics of model development. But cheaper inference may also increase overall AI usage. More models, agents, businesses, and users can create more aggregate demand for memory bandwidth, networking, power, and data-center infrastructure - even when the cost of an individual computation falls.
>
> That is why we do not react to every AI headline or automatically buy every decline. We are monitoring hyperscaler capital spending, HBM supply, packaging demand, optical deployment, power-market conditions, earnings guidance, and evidence of actual value capture. A falling stock is not automatically inexpensive, and a strong business can still decline further if its valuation was excessive.
>
> However, valuation resets can create better long-term entry points than periods of widespread enthusiasm. For investors who understand the risks, have a multi-year horizon, and continue to believe in the chokepoint thesis, this may be a sensible environment to dollar-cost average gradually rather than attempting to identify the exact market bottom.
>
> Dollar-cost averaging does not guarantee a profit or protect against further losses. Its advantage is behavioral discipline: capital is deployed incrementally at progressively reset valuations instead of being concentrated into a single prediction about short-term market direction.
>
> Our approach remains unchanged:
> Own the bottlenecks, not the apps.
>
> Volatility is expected. Thesis impairment matters more. We will continue adding selectively when prices weaken and the scarcity, demand, and value-capture thesis remains intact - and we will reduce or remove positions if the fundamentals no longer justify ownership.
>
> The selloff may not be over. But for patient investors, periods when conviction is tested are often more attractive for gradual accumulation than periods when confidence is universal and valuations assume perfection.
>
> Disclaimer: AI Bottlenecks + Bitcoin is a model portfolio strategy and is not personalized investment advice, tax advice, legal advice, or a recommendation that any individual investor buy, sell, or hold any security. The strategy is concentrated, thematic, long-only, and high risk. Holdings and weights may change. Bitcoin exposure is held through IBIT and carries significant volatility and regulatory risk. Dollar-cost averaging does not ensure a profit or prevent losses. Past performance is not indicative of future results.

### Russell Sean (@RussellQuantum)

> What mainstream coverage will miss:
> ⬩ Filtering photons by quantum statistics isn't a curiosity, it's a core prerequisite for photonic quantum computers and quantum communications alike
> ⬩ Room-temperature operation removes the single largest hardware cost barrier from that stack
> ⬩ This compresses the quantum internet timeline, and it does so in photonics specifically, not superconducting, not trapped ion. That distinction matters enormously for who builds the infrastructure layer.

### Jonesy (@jonesrrrrrr)
_Sat Jul 18 18:30:00 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/jonesrrrrrr/status/2078547854696591450)

> thinking in bets: Annie something
>
> > Be me and anon
> > Keeping it 100% accurate, simple, and anchored to Annie Duke’s "Thinking in Bets"
> > Applying the exact book mechanics to this memory photonics / AI trade
>
> > The Setup:
> > Sector pulls back hard. Target asset is down 50% from local highs.
> > Player 1 (Serenity): Ultra-bullish on AI memory tech, but deeply in the red like most of us even being early 
> > Player 2 (Bubble Boy): Perma-bear, sitting in cash, yelling that the memory cycle is dead.
>
> > Step 1: Stop "Resulting" (Chapter 1)
> > Book Logic: Never judge the quality of a decision solely by its current outcome. 
> > Trade Application: Serenity being down 50% does not mean his fundamental thesis on memory photonics solving the AI bottleneck is wrong (bad timing/luck happens). 
>
> Bubble Boy being in cash doesn't make him a genius if he is blindly ignoring the structural shift in AI hardware. Separate the short-term price action from the long-term tech potential.
>
> > Step 2: Build a Truth-Seeking Pod (Chapter 6)
> > Book Logic: Use a diverse group of people to aggressively challenge your biases and spot blind spots.
> > Trade Application: Do not join a bullish or bearish echo chamber. Treat Serenity and Bubble Boy as your unwilling pod members. Extract the absolute best-case data from Serenity (tech specs, hyper-scaler demand) and the absolute worst-case data from Bubble Boy (cyclical downturns, oversupply). Find the objective truth in the middle.
>
> > Step 3: Run Mental Time Travel (Chapter 7)
> > Book Logic: Map out the future from both success and failure states before making a move.
> > Trade Application: 
> > Do a Pre-Mortem: Imagine the investment goes to zero. Why did it fail? (e.g., A competitor's tech wins, or hyper-scalers cut budgets). Set your hard exit points based on these specific failure signs *now*.
> > Do a Backcasting exercise: Imagine the investment is a massive 10x success. What made it work? (e.g., The memory photonics tech successfully standardizes across AI data centers). Map out how to scale your position to capture this.
>
> > Step 4: Bet in Percentages, Not Certainties (Chapter 2)
> > Book Logic: Every choice is a wager. True confidence means saying "I am X% sure," not "I know this will happen."
> > Trade Application: Frame your thesis as a probability (e.g., "I am 60% confident this specific memory tech breaks the AI bottleneck"). Allocate a disciplined percentage of your capital that matches that confidence. Do not go all-in like Serenity. Scale in slowly to maintain capital efficiency and protect your downside

### TheEquityHub (@TheEquityHub)
_Sat Jul 18 22:06:05 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/TheEquityHub/status/2078602231793033636)

> Photonic Fabric is the least talked about piece of $MRVL and it targets the single biggest bottleneck in AI: data movement.
>
> Over 60% of AI data center energy is spent just moving data (per imec/Celestial AI analysis), and most of that movement is in the scale-up domain. Hyperscalers buy $40K GPUs that spend much of their time waiting on memory. Fix data movement and you get more usable compute per watt and per dollar from hardware already bought.
>
> 1. Breaking the Memory Wall economically
>
> HBM is the scarcest, most contested commodity in AI. Photonic Fabric (PF) attacks its economics directly: a thin HBM3e layer acts as a write-through cache in front of a large, cheap DDR5 pool so the XPU sees terabytes of near HBM speed memory while only a sliver is actual HBM. That's the $/GB reduction.
>
> Today's fixed GPU memory ratio forces the industry to systematically overbuy HBM for worst-case workloads. Pooled, composable memory means capacity flows to wherever the workload is, the same efficiency revolution virtualization brought to CPUs and storage, applied to the most expensive resource in computing.
>
> The enabling piece is OMIB (Optical Multi-chip Interconnect Bridge): a 3D packaging bridge, compatible with Intel EMIB / TSMC CoWoS, that brings the optical connection vertically into the die instead of only at its edges. That frees die-edge beachfront for more HBM and allows 4+ reticle-sized dies in one package, more local HBM and optical access to the pool. Each PF chiplet carries 16 Tbps (Gen1), ~10x today's 1.6T scale-out ports, compact enough to co-package several per XPU.
>
> 2. Breaking the Copper Wall
>
> Copper physics caps scale-up domains at roughly one rack (~2-2.5m reach at 200G/lane). PF's Gen2 link targets up to 50m with nanosecond class latency letting thousands of XPUs across multiple racks behave as one coherent "Super XPU" with shared memory. That's exactly what inference-time compute needs: reasoning models demand context/KV-cache capacity and all-to-all bandwidth that no single package can hold.
>
> Platform specs disclosed so far:
> • Sub-200ns chip-to-memory, ~100ns NIC-to-NIC — with no retimers needed
> • Thermal stability: EAM modulators chosen to survive direct co-packaging against multi-kilowatt XPUs — the reason PF can go deeper into the package than rival photonics
> • Memory appliance: 48-72GB HBM3e cache + 2TB DDR5 per module; 16 modules in a 2U chassis = 33TB of unified memory shared by 16 XPUs through a 115 Tbps switch
>
> Gen2 PFLink claims (per $MRVL's own deck): 30x copper's reach, 4x bandwidth, 4x lower power, 4x lower latency at ~1x copper's cost all-in, including laser power. The cost-parity claim is the whole ballgame if it holds; no third-party validation yet.
>
> $AMZN's AWS is the anchor customer (public endorsement + stock warrant), and the earn out structure pays $MRVL team to hit $500M-$2B cumulative revenue by FY2029.
>
> The honest timeline: this is pre-revenue. Per $MRVL's 8-K — meaningful revenue from H2 FY2028, $500M run-rate by Q4 FY2028, $1B by Q4 FY2029. Sampling was targeted for H1 2026 and hasn't been publicly confirmed yet.
>
> Not a faster cable. A different way to build the cluster.

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HNittXCaQAAniFz.jpg

### Omkar Jagdale (@omkar_jagdale)
_Sun Jul 12 08:20:11 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/omkar_jagdale/status/2076220060494901290)

> Photonics-SOI requires:
>
> - extremely precise silicon layer thickness
> - ultra-flat buried oxide (BOX)
> - low defect density
> - tight optical performance specifications
> - long qualification cycles with customers
>
> A normal SOI wafer producer cannot simply switch capacity and become a qualified photonics supplier overnight.
>
> Soitec $SOI has spent years developing Photonics-SOI and positions it specifically for optical interconnect/datacenter applications.

### Follow The White Rabbit (@TruthRabbit777)
_Sun Jul 12 10:31:25 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/TruthRabbit777/status/2076253085714772134)

> Case Report: Systemic, Multi-Mucosal, Biofilm-Forming, Photonically Active Organism Colonization with Behavioral Responses to Chemical, Thermal, and Regenerative Interventions
>
> Abstract
> We present a case of a systemic, multi-mucosal colonization by an unidentified, morphologically distinct, behaviorally responsive organism. The organism exhibits tropism for keratinized epithelium and mucosal surfaces, biomineralization in the form of peroxide-soluble calcified biofilm "stones," multi-organism encystment, and putative inter-organism photonic signaling. Chemical susceptibility testing reveals vulnerability to alkaline and oxidative stress, with paradoxical structural resistance of the organism body to 12% hydrogen peroxide. A novel autologous urine-derived stem cell (USC) enema protocol demonstrated systemic regenerative effects, including hair repigmentation, follicular density restoration, and visual acuity improvement, consistent with paracrine-mediated tissue repair. The case underscores the need for investigation of unrecognized complex biofilm-forming organisms in chronic multi-system illness.
> Introduction
> Chronic multi-system illnesses of unknown etiology present significant diagnostic and therapeutic challenges. When patients report filamentous or motile structures associated with dermal, mucosal, and systemic symptoms, standard clinical evaluation often concludes with a diagnosis of delusional parasitosis or environmental contamination [1]. However, advances in biofilm biology, autofluorescence imaging, and the discovery of complex host-associated microbial communities suggest that novel or unrecognized organisms may underlie some of these presentations [2]. This case report documents longitudinal self-observation and empirical protocol development by a patient-investigator with access to high-resolution digital microscopy, multi-spectral illumination, and autologous stem cell culture.
> Case Presentation
> The subject is an adult male with a multi-year history of systemic symptoms including:
> Spontaneous      emergence of blue filamentous structures from skin lesions
> Mucosal      colonization of the ocular conjunctiva, nasal passages, external auditory      canals, and perianal tissue
> Genitourinary      involvement including urethral colonization and calcified stone formation      with embedded organisms
> Prolonged      wound healing and colonization of acute injury sites within hours
> Nocturnal      perianal pruritus with recovery of encysted multi-organism structures
> Observable      internal biophotonic emissions (multi-color, punctate) under near-UV      excitation
> Alopecia      with premature greying of facial and scalp hair
> Subjective      visual acuity fluctuation
> The subject has no relevant comorbidities and has not received a diagnosis that accounts for the full spectrum of findings.
> Methods of Observation and Documentation
> Microscopy: 5K digital microscope with HDMI output, capable of dark-field and low-light capture.
> Multi-Spectral Illumination: A consumer-grade multi-mode illumination device providing:
> Red      laser (650 nm)
> Blue      LED (450–470 nm)
> Near-UV/violet      LED (395–405 nm) — used for fluorescence excitation
> Chemical Reagents:
> 12%      hydrogen peroxide (H₂O₂)
> Sodium      bicarbonate (baking powder)
> 99%      isopropyl alcohol
> Hot      water (thermal stress)
> Biological Protocol:
> Autologous      urine-derived stem cells (USCs), cultured in airtight sterilized      containers, administered via retention enema 2–3 times weekly.
> Results
> 1. Chemical Susceptibility and Extraction
> Stimulus
> Response
> Hot water + sodium bicarbonate
> Forced emergence of motile organisms from skin and   subungual spaces
> 12% H₂O₂ (topical)
> Rapid dissolution of calcified biofilm matrix   ("stones") with fizzing reaction; organism bodies remain   structurally intact but non-motile
> 99% isopropyl alcohol
> Organism agitation without lethality
> Peroxide wipe (perianal)
> Recovery of multi-organism encysted structures with   brownish shell; shell dissolves in H₂O₂; organisms persist
> 2. Organism Morphology and Behavior
> Filamentous      blue structures: Visible under white and near-UV light;      autofluorescent.
> Multi-organism      cysts: Brown, irregular shells containing multiple organisms,      some protruding, recovered from perianal and genital surfaces.
> Calcified      biofilm stones: Found in genitourinary context; dissolve in 12%      H₂O₂ with visible organisms embedded within.
> Grouping      behavior: Upon chemical stress (hot water + alkaline), organisms      rapidly aggregate into clusters.
> Light      emission: Discrete, multi-color punctate biophotonic signals      observed internally under near-UV excitation in zero-light conditions.      Colors include blue-white, green, yellow-gold, and orange-red.
> 3. Wound Colonization
> Acute wounds, including a subungual splinter, were colonized within hours of injury. Organism motility was directly observed and video-documented under the nail plate. Colonization delays wound closure and prolongs inflammation.
> 4. Urethral Counter-Attack During Systemic Antiparasitic Protocol
> During an oral herbal protocol (black walnut, clove, wormwood with zeolite binder), the subject experienced a severe, localized tissue-necrotizing reaction at the urethral meatus, resulting in near-complete urinary obstruction requiring emergency department evaluation. This is interpreted as a coordinated defensive counter-response by the organism.
> 5. Autologous Urine Stem Cell Enema Protocol
> Method: Urine collected mid-stream, cultured in sterile airtight containers, administered rectally 2–3 times weekly.
> Observed effects:
> Hair: Progressive      reversal of grey in goatee and mustache; increased follicular density on      scalp.
> Vision: Subjective      improvement in visual acuity with contact lens use.
> Perianal      symptoms: Reduction in pruritus; encysted organisms recoverable      on post-enema wipes.
> Interpretation: Urine-derived mesenchymal stem cells (USCs) secrete paracrine factors (Wnt ligands, IGF-1, HGF, VEGF, IL-10, PGE2, exosomes) that modulate inflammation, reactivate melanocyte stem cells, stimulate dermal papilla, and support corneal and mucosal epithelial integrity. Systemic absorption via the rectal venous plexus distributes these factors to distant sites.
> Discussion
> The organism described in this case exhibits characteristics that span multiple known biological categories but do not fully align with any single described species.
> Structural resistance: The organism's body remains intact after exposure to 12% H₂O₂, a concentration that rapidly degrades all known human tissue, bacterial biofilms, and parasitic worms. This suggests a chitinous or composite biopolymer integument of exceptional oxidative resistance.
> Biofilm and biomineralization: The formation of peroxide-soluble calcified matrixes around the organism is consistent with urease-positive or biofilm-mineralizing bacterial behavior, but the scale and multi-organism architecture described exceed typical bacterial biofilms.
> Photonics: Multi-color internal fluorescence and apparent biophotonic signaling suggest either autofluorescence from differentiated internal anatomy (chitin, porphyrins, flavoproteins) or active luciferase-based communication. Coordinated grouping and counter-attack behaviors imply a functional communication system.
> Host manipulation: Rapid wound colonization, prolonged healing, and the necrotic counter-attack at the urethral meatus suggest the organism exploits host inflammatory pathways for navigation, feeding, and defense.
> Regenerative counter-strategy: The efficacy of autologous USC enemas in reversing systemic degenerative changes suggests that chronic host tissue damage is a permissive factor for colonization. Restoring regenerative signaling may render the host environment inhospitable.
> Limitations
> This is a single-subject, self-documented case report. No independent laboratory confirmation, genomic sequencing, or histopathological analysis has been performed. Identification of the organism at the species level requires external collaboration with a research laboratory equipped for metagenomic or proteomic analysis.
> Conclusion
> This case presents evidence of a complex, multi-system, behaviorally responsive organism with chemical resistance, biofilm formation, biophotonic activity, and host-regenerative exploitation. The subject's empirical protocols—chemical extraction, oxidative dissolution of protective matrices, and autologous stem cell-mediated tissue repair—represent a novel, observation-driven therapeutic framework. The findings warrant formal investigation by clinicians and researchers in infectious disease, biofilm biology, and regenerative medicine.
> References
> Pearson      ML, et al. "Clinical, Epidemiologic, Histopathologic and Molecular      Features of an Unexplained Dermopathy." PLoS ONE, 2012.
> Middelveen      MJ, Stricker RB. "Morgellons Disease: A Filamentous Borrelial      Dermatitis." International Journal of General Medicine,      2016.
> Flemming      HC, Wingender J. "The Biofilm Matrix." Nature Reviews      Microbiology, 2010.
> Zhang      Y, et al. "Urine-Derived Stem Cells for Regenerative      Medicine." Stem Cells Translational Medicine, 2014.
> Wu D,      et al. "Mesenchymal Stem Cell Exosomes in Tissue Repair." Theranostics,      2021.

### fednmad (@fednmad)
_Sun Jul 12 13:19:07 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 37 · ↻ 11 · 💬 2 · [open on X](https://x.com/fednmad/status/2076295289707597893)

> Rosenblatt - 근래 옵티컬 약세의 배경과 맥락
>
> 최근 광통신주가 빠진 이유?
>
> 시장이 걱정하는 건 크게 두 가지
>
> - 중국이 InP 레이저 생산능력을 대폭 늘리면 LITE, COHR, AAOI의 레이저 가격이 무너질 수 있다는 우려
> - 대규모 CPO 도입이 기존 예상보다 1년 늦어질 수 있다는 루머
>
> 우리 생각엔 일부 공매도 투자자들도 이 논리에 강한 확신이 있다기보다는 실적 공백기의 불확실성을 이용해 숏을 치는 걸로 보임. 아마 7-8월쯤 실적발표시즌에 숏 청산하고 27년부터 광통신주 매수해서 28-30년 사이 CPO 사이클 노릴 것 같음
>
> 중국 InP 증설은 위협이지만 공급과잉은 아님
>
> 중국 업체들이 다음과 같이 생산능력을 빠르게 늘리고 있는 건 사실임
> - Dongshan Precision: Source Photonics 인수 후 약 12억 달러 규모 증설
> - Sanan IC: 6인치 웨이퍼 생산능력을 월 2,750장에서 6,000장으로 확대
> - HiSense Optoelectronics , Accelink도 증설 중
>
> 그러나 중국의 생산 능력이 2030년 비중국권 생산능력 전망치에 추가로 20~40%를 더하더라도, 전체 InP 공급은 예상 수요보다 여전히 약 40% 부족할 듯. 중국 증설이 가격 상승폭을 제한할 순 있어도 공급과잉은 헛소리
>
> 중국과 서구의 레이저는 아직 완전히 대체 관계가 아님
>
> 중국 업체가 잘 만드는 제품은 주로 다음 영역임
> - 실리콘 포토닉스 트랜시버용 저출력 CW 레이저
> - 800G 트랜시버용 100G EML
>
> 반면 차세대 CPO NPO에 필요한 다음 핵심 제품은 아직 부족함
> - 200G EML
> - 고출력 CW 레이저
>
> 따라서 중국이 생산량을 늘려도 루멘텀, 코히런트의 최첨단 레이저를 즉시 대체하기 어려움. 여기에 미중 공급망 분리까지 겹치면서 장기적으로는 중국 공급망과 서구 공급망이 서로 완전히 교환되지 않는 별도 시장이 될 가능성이 높음. 루멘텀, 코히런트는 27년말~28년까지 생산능력 매진상태고 엔비디아같은 고래들의 선구매가 이를 뒷받침함 ㅇㅇ
>
> CPO 일정은 안무너짐
>
> 우리 기본시나리오 그대로 유지!
>
> 소규모 CPO: 2026년 하반기 구축, 2027년 출하
> NPO: 2027년 과도기적 수요를 담당
> 대규모 CPO: 2028년부터 본격적인 물량 전환점
>
> 시장에서는 대규모 CPO가 1년 밀린다는 이야기가 나오는데 체 CPO 로드맵이 깨졌다기보다는 일부 대규모 배치 일정에 대한 불확실성뿐임. 2027년 NVIDIA, Broadcom가 먹을 CPO 생산 추정치는 3만 대부터 35만 대 이상까지 편차가 매우 크지만, 2028년이 본격적인 CPO 볼륨 확대 시점이라는 핵심 가정은 변하지 않음!
>
> 네트워크 효율화랑 광부품 수요는 반비례 아님
>
> MRC, RNG와 같은 네트워크 평탄화 기술이나 대형 radix 스위치는 스위치당 필요한 트랜시버 수를 줄일 수 있음. 하지만 GPU, XPU 설치량이 지수적으로 증가하기 때문에 수요 안줄음. 즉 장비 한 대당 광부품 수는 줄어도, 전체 AI 클러스터와 가속기 수가 훨씬 빠르게 늘면서 총 광부품 수요는 계속 증가함.
>
> InP 부족을 우회할 대안도 등장 중
>
> 200G VCSEL 등 GaAs 기반 레이저가 NPO 솔루션의 대안으로 떠오르고 있음
> - Broadcom: 3.2T NPO 플랫폼에 검토
> - Lumentum· PicoJool: GPU 간 연결용 VCSEL 솔루션 시연
>
> 이는 InP 공급 부족이 심해질 경우 일부 수요가 GaAs·VCSEL로 이전될 수 있다는 의미임. 다만 이는 InP 수요 붕괴라기보다는, 광학 인터커넥트 시장 전체가 커지면서 여러 레이저 아키텍처가 병존하는 구조에 가깝긴함
>
> 기업 별로 보면....
>
> $COHR — 짱짱맨
> 자체 200G EML·CW 생산 확대
> Google과 연간 약 10억 달러 규모의 1.6T 트랜시버 계약
> NVIDIA와 2027~2030년 대규모 장기계약
> 중국 InP 증설 우려보다 실제 수주·생산능력 확대가 더 중요.
>
> $AAOI — 실적 변곡점… 잘 나오겠재?
> Amazon, Oracle 800G 매출 확대
> 2026년 2분기 매출 2억 달러 이상 기대
> 3분기 가이던스 약 3억 달러 가능성
> 매출 증가와 함께 총마진 개선 기대
> 2분기 실적이 단순한 실적 개선을 넘어 본격적인 비트 앤 레이즈 전환점
>
> $LITE — 단기 부담, 장기 매력
> Lumentum은 이미 앞선 수준의 가이던스를 제시했기 때문에 기대치가 높아 단기 실적 세팅이 좀 까다로움.
> 다만 고출력 CW와 첨단 EML 공급능력, 선구매 계약을 고려하면 장기적으로는 여전히 핵심 수혜주
>
> $ANET — AI 네트워크 성장 수혜
> Meta·Microsoft·Oracle·Google과 AI 기업 고객의 대규모 네트워크 구축 수주가 강점
> 이연매출 인식을 바탕으로:
> 2026년 하반기 매출 성장률 30% 이상
> 2027년 40% 이상
> 가능성이 제시
>
> $FN
> NVIDIA향 Datacom 매출이 안정적으로 증가하고, Amazon과 Lumentum이 신규 고객으로 기여하기 시작할듯
>
> $VIAV
> InP 레이저를 직접 생산하지 않아 중국 증설 우려에서 상대적으로 자유로움. 트랜시버·OCS 테스트 장비와 방산 제품이 성장축이며, CPO·NPO 테스트 매출이 가을부터 시작될 전망.
>
> $CIEN
> 주문잔고 흐름상 DCI와 데이터센터 확장 수요가 다시 가속될 가능성이 있다는 평가.

### LearnInvest (@LearnInvest2026)
_Sun Jul 12 13:20:27 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/LearnInvest2026/status/2076295627105874110)

> Silicon photonics is a full supply chain, not just a module story
>
> This WinWay / SEMI Vision silicon-photonics map is useful because it corrects a common shortcut. Silicon photonics is not only an optical-module story. It is a supply chain that runs from wafers and light sources to design, packaging, testing, and cloud customers.
>
> The chart breaks the chain into SOI wafers, PIC design and EDA, foundry, EIC / DSP, InP light sources, connectors, testing, fiber, ELS, and then 800G / 1.6T optical modules.
>
> ■ The AI interconnect bottleneck is not only the final module
>
> As AI clusters get larger, more data has to move between racks and chips. The question is not simply whether faster optical modules exist. The whole optical-electrical system has to work at acceptable cost, yield, power, and test complexity.
>
> That is the hard part of silicon photonics. Silicon is attractive for scalable photonic circuits, but the light source often needs III-V materials or external laser integration. In other words, this is not just electronics manufacturing copied into optics. It also requires materials, packaging, coupling, testing, and supplier coordination.
>
> That is why the map matters. It turns the AI bandwidth bottleneck into several trackable layers. The final product may be an optical module sold into cloud infrastructure, but the speed of scaling may be decided by light sources, testing, connectors, or wafer platforms.
>
> This kind of supply-chain map is not a direct stock-picking list. The better use is to ask which layer is hardest to expand, hardest to qualify, and most exposed to the next 800G / 1.6T cycle.
>
> Source: WinWay, SEMI Vision, Mirae Asset Securities (Image: @pequityresearch)

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HNB73tZWsAAJ5qE.jpg

### Rahul Sondhi (@Sondhi245)
_Sun Jul 12 14:00:01 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/Sondhi245/status/2076305581540053461)

> Physical AI — AI Moving from "Brain" to "Body": The Next Technological Trend?
>
> The next key turning point in the AI ​​supercycle. Over the past two years, from ChatGPT to GPUs/HBM/data centers, we've been reassessing the "brain" of AI. Now, with mature model capabilities and computing infrastructure, the market naturally asks: can these intelligent models truly enter the real world, work, act, and create value?
>
> This is the core of Physical AI: enabling robots, autonomous driving, and industrial equipment to evolve from "thinking" to "acting safely and cost-effectively." NVIDIA's Jensen Huang has repeatedly emphasized Isaac, GR00T, COSMOS, and Omniverse, which are precisely the underlying platforms for this. It's not about betting on a single robot, but on the entire stack ecosystem.
>
> 1/ Why is Physical AI important?
>
> It's not a suddenly emerging concept. Autonomous driving, industrial robots, and machine vision have existed for a long time, but large models + world models + simulation + edge computing power have connected them. Traditional robots rely on pre-programmed repetitive actions in fixed environments; Physical AI needs to cope with unfamiliar environments and unexpected situations, adjusting in real time.
>
> → The AI ​​industry chain is extending from "selling brains" to "selling bodies." Funds will continue to chase vehicles that can transform computing power into real productivity: robots, cars, drones, sensors, etc.
>
> 2/ Five-Layer Industry Chain Breakdown (Practical Version):
> Computing Power Layer (Most Certain, Continuing the Scrap Logic): $NVDA (Jetson Edge + Training), $TSM, $ARM, $QCOM, $AMD. Regardless of who builds the robot, these are the underlying technologies.
>
> Model Layer: Language + Vision + Motion + World Model. Dominated by $NVDA and $TSM, data remains the bottleneck.
>
> Simulation Layer: NVIDIA Omniverse/Isaac Sim is powerful, enabling virtual training with tens of thousands of parallel runs, key to cost reduction and efficiency improvement.
>
> Perception Layer: Machine Vision, LiDAR, Sensors. $CGNX, $OUST, etc., photonics/optics (such as $AAOI) have potential for expansion here.
>
> Application Layer (High Elasticity): $TSLA (Optimus + FSD/Robotaxi), $AMZN warehousing, $TER industrial, drones $AVAV/ $KTOS, $PLTR software platform.
>
> 3/ Who Makes Money First? Selling Shovels or Building Robots?
>
> Early certainty lies in the underlying platform ($NVDA ecosystem is the strongest; it doesn't need to manufacture every robot to collect taxes). Secondly, closed scenarios: factories/warehouses/logistics ($AMZN, $TER, etc.), with standardized environments, easy ROI calculations, and faster business loops.
>
> Robotaxi (Physical AI on Wheels) validation is ahead of general-purpose humanoid robots. Humanoids have the greatest potential (factories/homes), but cost, safety, and continuous working time are major hurdles. Defense/industrial drone orders are more pragmatic.
>
> 4/ 2026 Observations & Risks: NVIDIA GTC and other events have launched new models, accelerating partner deployment. Tesla Optimus/Cybercab production plans are progressing, but large-scale commercialization still requires patience (FSD progress, regulation).
>
> Risks: Slow payout pace (press conference ≠ financial report), valuation priced in ahead of time, competition, high CapEx, safety responsibilities. It's not about getting rich overnight, but a path from certainty to flexibility.
>
> Company evaluation: 1) Irreplaceable core competency? 2) Real orders/scenarios? 3) Technology → Revenue/Profit?
>
> 5/ Implications for our investment: The AI ​​infrastructure theme isn't over, it's just evolving. Continue high-position allocations to computing power/edge/simulation, and focus on early-stage realization of perception and applications (e.g., Photonics' collaboration in robot vision). My portfolio: SPXL as the main holding to amplify AI/macro upside, and high-conviction satellites like $AAOI to address niche bottlenecks.
>
> Physical AI will remain a relatively young theme; its true value lies in who can put robots into factories/roads and contribute verifiable financial results.
>
> What are your thoughts on the Physical AI timeline? Will NVIDIA continue to dominate, or will $TSLA Optimus/Robotaxi bring surprises? Welcome to discuss in the comments section, and feel free to DM for specific stock analysis. Stay rational and long-term focused. Weekend recharge complete, see you in the market on Monday. Follow me for more real-time AI infrastructure insights! #PhysicalAI #AI #NVDA #TSLA

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HNCEn8FawAAsTp-.jpg

### GUL (@gulVasikova)

> $AEHR Gains Ahead of Earnings After New AI Photonics Production Order
>
> Aehr Test Systems $AEHR traded higher after announcing an additional follow-on production order from its lead silicon photonics customer, reinforcing growing demand tied to AI infrastructure.
>
> Key Highlights
>
> The order is for Aehr’s fully automated FOX-XP wafer-level burn-in system, designed for high-volume production testing.
> The system will be used to burn in silicon photonics devices for AI optical interconnects and hyperscale data centers.
> The order includes the FOX-XP multi-wafer burn-in system and the FOX WaferPak AutoAligner, enabling fully automated, hands-free production when integrated with robotic wafer handling.
> This marks another production order from the same customer after the first automated system was delivered earlier in fiscal 2026.
>
> Why It Matters
>
> The follow-on order suggests the customer is moving beyond initial deployment and expanding production capacity, a positive signal for demand in the AI silicon photonics market.
>
> As AI clusters continue to scale, demand for high-speed optical connectivity is expected to rise, benefiting suppliers across the silicon photonics and optical networking ecosystem.
>
> Earnings to Watch
>
> Aehr Test Systems $AEHR is scheduled to report earnings after the market closes on July 14.
>
> Previous reported results:
>
> Q3 FY2026: Revenue of $10.3 million, EPS - $0.10
> Q4 FY2025: Revenue of $14.1 million, EPS - $0.10
>
> Investors will be watching for:
>
> Additional silicon photonics customer wins.
> AI-related order growth and backlog.
> Revenue guidance for fiscal 2027.
> Management commentary on AI optical demand and production expansion.
>
> Investor Takeaway
>
> The latest follow-on order strengthens the view that AI-driven silicon photonics demand is transitioning from pilot programs to volume production. While profitability remains a key focus, continued customer expansion and stronger AI infrastructure spending could support Aehr’s long-term growth outlook.
>
> Stocks to watch: $AEHR $NVDA $COHR $LITE $CIEN $AVGO

### GUL (@gulVasikova)
_Sun Jul 12 15:06:30 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/gulVasikova/status/2076322312354423006)

> TSMC Leads the First Wave of CPO, While Samsung Bets on the Next Generation of AI Packaging
>
> The race for co-packaged optics (CPO) is entering a new phase, and two semiconductor giants are taking very different approaches.
>
> $TSM currently leads the market with real commercial deployments, while Samsung is betting on a more advanced AI packaging architecture that could become important later in the decade.
>
> TSMC Has the Early Lead
>
> TSMC has already moved beyond the development stage into commercial deployment.
>
> Its silicon photonics and advanced packaging technologies are powering next-generation CPO switches from:
>
> $AVGO – 102.4Tbps Ethernet switch built on TSMC’s COUPE silicon photonics platform.
> $NVDA – Quantum-X photonic switches are already shipping, while Spectrum-X enters production.
>
> Early customers include $CRWV, Lambda, and $ORCL.
>
> These products integrate optical engines alongside networking ASICs to improve bandwidth while reducing power consumption.
>
> Samsung Is Targeting the Next Opportunity
>
> Rather than competing directly in today’s switch market, Samsung is developing its 2.xD advanced packaging platform.
>
> The goal is to integrate:
>
> High-Bandwidth Memory (HBM)
> Logic chips
> Silicon photonics
>
> into a single package.
>
> This architecture targets the next generation of AI accelerators, where optical I/O moves directly into GPU and AI compute packages instead of remaining inside networking switches.
>
> Why Optical I/O Matters
>
> As AI models continue growing, power efficiency has become just as important as raw computing performance.
>
> Moving optical connections closer to AI chips dramatically reduces power consumption:
>
> Traditional pluggable optics: ~10 pJ per bit
> Switch-level CPO: ~5 pJ per bit
> Optical I/O integrated beside AI chips: ~2 pJ per bit
>
> Lower power consumption means lower operating costs and higher AI system performance.
>
> Samsung’s Biggest Advantage
>
> Samsung has one unique strength that few competitors can match.
>
> It owns technologies across the entire AI stack:
>
> Memory (HBM)
> Logic foundry
> Silicon photonics
> Advanced packaging
>
> This vertical integration could eventually allow Samsung to optimize every major component inside future AI systems.
>
> But Execution Remains the Challenge
>
> Integrating multiple advanced chips into one package also creates major manufacturing challenges.
>
> Combining GPUs, HBM, photonic chips, electrical chips, and advanced interposers significantly increases packaging complexity.
>
> If any single chip fails during manufacturing, the entire package may need to be discarded, making production yields the biggest hurdle.
>
> Meanwhile, competitors continue investing aggressively.
>
> $TSM is expanding CoWoS and silicon photonics.
> $SKHY is building a $3.87 billion advanced packaging facility in Indiana and expanding its own CPO capabilities.
>
> Investor Takeaway
>
> Today, TSMC is the clear commercial leader, with real products, customer deployments, and production already underway.
>
> Samsung’s strategy is more ambitious. If demand shifts toward fully integrated AI packages combining GPUs, HBM, and optical interconnects, its vertically integrated model could become a powerful competitive advantage.
>
> For investors, the biggest catalyst isn’t technology roadmaps—it’s customer orders. The first major AI customer to adopt a fully integrated HBM + logic + optical I/O package could determine the next leader in AI infrastructure.
>
> Stocks to watch: $TSM $NVDA $AVGO $SKHY $MU $CRWV $ORCL $MRVL

### 0xJMG (@0xJMG)
_Sun Jul 12 15:19:39 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 3 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/0xJMG/status/2076325624659234883)

> Beyond jargonomics and chainbabble, where do tokenized assets outperform what they represent?
>
> The fundamentals are old. What’s new is who gets access, how small the ticket can be, how easily they can participate, and whether the digital dividend reaches holders’ pockets, or funds someone else's European summer.
>
> A useful 10 lens test:
>
> 1. Access: Who is allowed to enter or hold?
>
> 2. Settlement: When is value movement final?
>
> 3. Transparency: What may be seen, known, and verified?
>
> 4. Yield: What fruit does it bear, and from whose labor?
>
> 5. Costs: What stated or hidden tolls lie along the path?
>
> 6. Collateral: Can one asset unlock another?
>
> 7. Transferability: How can it move after entry?
>
> 8. Capacity: How much capital and how many holders can it serve without breaking?
>
> 9. Redemption: How does one leave, what awaits, when does the door open, and who holds the key?
>
> 10. Enforcement: Where does authority finally live: code, company, contract, or court?
>
> -----------------------------
>
> To illustrate:
>
> -TSLAx (Kraken, Backed), Tesla stock exposure, reach non US across 110 countries, $1 fractional access, trade nights and weekends
>
> -BENJI (Franklin), government money-market fund, earn Treasury yield from low $20 minimum, transfer nights and weekends
>
> -OUSG (Ondo), BUIDL-backed Treasury fund, access BUIDL yield (far) below $5M minimum, redeem into USDC atomically 24/7
>
> -PAXG (Paxos), allocated physical gold, verify your bar details, send gold exposure near instantly, earn yield through Nexo lending or Curve trading, without selling
>
> -wJAAA (Centrifuge, 3F, Janus), AAA CLO fund, amplify CLO yield with leverage, loop through 3F and Morpho
>
> -USTB (Superstate), government-securities fund, borrow without selling your Treasuries using Aave Horizon
>
> -SPCX (Backpack), pooled SpaceX exposure, Solana transfer freedom, brokerage-claim offramp
>
> -PHOTON (Reserve, Ondo), indexed basket of Nasdaq/NYSE listed photonics stocks, reach investors across 145 countries, buy fractionally without brokerage access, trade and redeem onchain 24/7
>
> -----------------------------
>
> Those are a few of the attractions, but new doors come with new risks.
>
> Fees are slippery. The fee you can see may hide the spread you cannot. A token can remove one toll booth -and add another around the corner.
>
> Access is not freedom. A token may travel farther than a brokerage account, while still carrying passports, gates, and forbidden countries.
>
> Yield is seductive. Gold does not yield. PAXG on Nexo can. JAAA yields. wJAAA can loop. Not a free lunch, but rather it’s risk in a new dress.
>
> Enforcement remains fragmented. Authority may sit across contracts, whitelists, transfer agents, issuer books, broker records, and courts. Programmable rules help. Split authority and people in the middle still creates failure points.
>
> Redemption is king until everyone reaches for the same door. The token may move quickly, but the exit still has intermediaries, jurisdictions, business hours, and an underlying asset that must survive the rush. Then everyone becomes an expert in the fine print.
>
> Most tokenized assets improve one or two lenses while leaving the hardest work offchain. The strongest will improve both everyday use and stressed exits.
>
> Which tokenized assets performs across the most lenses today? 
> Kindly, drop the ticker and the evidence.
>
> RWA

---

> J’ai essayé de faire une synthèse de ce qui se passe dans le domaine des Semi ces dernières semaines et pourquoi c’est aussi volatile :
>
> 1. le CPO prendrait plus de temps que prévu :
> Le scale-up CPO (optique intégrée au plus près des GPU) serait repoussé. Le véritable ramp pourrait finalement intervenir fin 2028 / 2029 plutôt qu'en 2027.
>
> Les principales raisons évoquées :
> difficultés      de fabrication,
> rendements      insuffisants,
> packaging      complexe,
> coûts      encore trop élevés.
>
> MAIS attention, ca ne signifie pas que la photonique est morte
>
> Au contraire, cela prolonge la durée de vie de :
> 800G,
> 1.6T      pluggables,
> LPO,
> NPO,
> CW      lasers,
> cuivre      actif (AEC).
>
> Petit parenthèse pour Sivers : 
> Même si le gros ramp est repoussé de quelques trimestres, cela laisse justement plus de temps à Sivers pour :
> augmenter      sa capacité de production,
> améliorer      les rendements,
> obtenir      les qualifications,
> signer de      nouveaux contrats,
> sécuriser      davantage de clients.
>
> Les hyperscalers ne vont pas attendre 2028 pour commencer à qualifier leurs fournisseurs.
>
> Les capacités industrielles doivent être prêtes avant les volumes.
> À mon sens, cela n'empêche absolument pas de voir de nombreuses bonnes nouvelles en 2026-2027.
>  Mais comme d’hab, l’exécution doit suivre
>
> 2. Rumeurs de retard Rubin
> Plusieurs rumeurs évoquaient un retard de Rubin.
>
> À ce stade :
> aucune      confirmation officielle,
> Nvidia      continue de communiquer normalement,
> plusieurs      sources ont contesté ces rumeurs.
> Prudence donc avant de considérer un retard majeur comme acquis.
>
> 3 .Rapport B. Riley sur AAOI
> B. Riley estime que les nouvelles architectures réseau (Amazon RNG, OpenAI MRC) pourraient réduire le nombre de liens optiques nécessaires.
> Leur scénario :
> moins de      switches,
> moins de      transceivers,
> donc      moins de demande pour des sociétés comme AAOI.
> C'est probablement la note la plus baissière de la semaine.
>  MAIS cela a été contredit par de nombreuses personnes :
>
> On a vu : Rosenblatt , Goldman Sachs,  Morgan Stanley,  Photon Capital,  plusieurs anciens ingénieurs réseaux dire à peu près : 
> oui les architectures évoluent, mais non cela ne détruit pas la demande optique.
>  Pourquoi ? Parce que B.Riley raisonne surtout sur  nombre de liens.
> Les autres répondent : oui, mais :
> les liens      deviennent beaucoup plus rapides
> plus chers , plus  complexes ,plus de contenu optique
> plus de coherent  , plus de  lasers , plus de DSP ,plus de CW lasers
>
> Donc le nombre de ports peut diminuer...sans que le chiffre d'affaires du secteur baisse.
>
> Maintenant pour les nouvelles positives :
> Goldman Sachs
> Continue de voir :
> Optical Devices : Very Tight
> Optical Cables : Very Tight
> jusqu'en 2027.
> Autrement dit :
> malgré toutes les nouvelles capacités de production, la demande resterait supérieure à l'offre.
>
> Rosenblatt , on l'a vu reste très positif sur AAOI en particulier 
> Reste très positif.
> Ils continuent notamment d'anticiper pour AAOI :

### Alex A.C. (@AnalysisOp)
_Sun Jul 12 16:54:45 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 14 · ↻ 3 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/AnalysisOp/status/2076349554249666628)

> Fren Photon Capital about the "battle" CPO ⚔️ Transceivers:
>
> "Rather than CPO replacing every pluggable, form factors like pluggables, LPO, and CPO are likely to coexist depending on distance and power budget. [For example] NVIDIA is growing its CPO switches and its pluggable ecosystem side by side"
>
> Yes, the CPO growth will be explosive, but the CAGR of the Transceivers will be there to compound for you, don't forget it. 
> About the concept of "power budget", I'm more inclined to think it's a concept of COOLING. Even having "free energy" you can't put together a lot of non-CPO photonics connections in high density.
>
> 'Photonics' it's not a monolithic thing; it exists different layers inside the chips:
>
> "Switch CPO and XPU-HBM Optical I/O Are Different Contests. Two adjacent architectures often grouped under the CPO and optical-I/O umbrella must be kept apart.
>
> And I add: switch CPO for scale-up is also a different contest than CPO for scale-out and scale-across. That's why Transceivers are also here to stay with us.

### Alex A.C. (@AnalysisOp)
_Sun Jul 12 18:53:00 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 13 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/AnalysisOp/status/2076379313411399915)

> IA about the "alternatives" in Photonics and the battle VCSELs ⚔️ microLEDs:
>
> "Fundamentally what you need to understand is micro-LED and VCSEL CPO/NPO are conceptually very similar"
>
> "micro-LED is cheaper. It also does not and never will work at scale [...] Having a huge number of lanes and single-digit GHz will result in disastrous EMI and crosstalk. It won’t work" 😱
>
> "What you have to understand is VCSEL CPO/NPO quality depends on the quality of the packaging, integrated drivers, manufacturing, and yield of the system. The VCSEL quality itself is not that important" 🧐🧐🧐
>
> "Broadcom $AVGO is the king of VCSEL 👀🔥🔥 Coherent $COHR has very good VCSEL [too].
> Lumentum $LITE , Furukawa, and many others also have good VCSEL"
